<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Great Depression</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Worldwide economic depression (1929–1939)</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the severe worldwide economic downturn in the 1930s. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/The_Great_Depression_(disambiguation)" title="The Great Depression (disambiguation)">The Great Depression (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="8066" data-file-width="6205" decoding="async" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg/260px-Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg/390px-Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg/520px-Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dorothea_Lange" title="Dorothea Lange">Dorothea Lange</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Migrant_Mother" title="Migrant Mother">Migrant Mother</a></i> depicts destitute <a href="/wiki/Pea-pickers" title="Pea-pickers">pea pickers</a> in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, centering on <a href="/wiki/Florence_Owens_Thompson" title="Florence Owens Thompson">Florence Owens Thompson</a>, age 32, a mother of seven children, in <a href="/wiki/Nipomo,_California" title="Nipomo, California">Nipomo, California</a>, March 1936.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Unemployment_from_1910-1960.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="339" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/US_Unemployment_from_1910-1960.svg/330px-US_Unemployment_from_1910-1960.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/US_Unemployment_from_1910-1960.svg/495px-US_Unemployment_from_1910-1960.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/US_Unemployment_from_1910-1960.svg/660px-US_Unemployment_from_1910-1960.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Unemployment_from_1910-1960.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The unemployment rate in the U.S. during 1910–60, with the years of the Great Depression (1929–39) highlighted</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1929_wall_street_crash_graph.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/1929_wall_street_crash_graph.svg/400px-1929_wall_street_crash_graph.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/1929_wall_street_crash_graph.svg/600px-1929_wall_street_crash_graph.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/1929_wall_street_crash_graph.svg/800px-1929_wall_street_crash_graph.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1929_wall_street_crash_graph.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>, 1928–1930</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Great Depression</b> was a severe worldwide <a href="/wiki/Economic_depression" title="Economic depression">economic depression</a> between 1929 and 1939<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> that began after a major fall in stock prices in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Financial_contagion" title="Financial contagion">economic contagion</a> began around September 4, 1929, and became known worldwide on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Tuesday" title="Black Tuesday">Black Tuesday</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_crash" title="Stock market crash">stock market crash</a> of October 29, 1929. The economic shock transmitted across the world, impacting countries to varying degrees, with most countries experiencing the Great Depression from 1929. The Great Depression was the longest, deepest, and most widespread depression of the 20th century<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-3">[3]</a></sup> and is regularly used as an example of an intense global economic depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 1929 and 1932, worldwide <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product (GDP)</a> fell by an estimated 15%. By comparison, worldwide GDP fell by less than 1% from 2008 to 2009 during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Some economies started to recover by the mid-1930s. However, in many countries, the negative effects of the Great Depression lasted until the beginning of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Devastating effects were seen in both rich and poor countries with falling <a href="/wiki/Personal_income" title="Personal income">personal income</a>, prices, tax revenues, profits and prices. International trade fell by more than 50%, unemployment in the U.S. rose to 23% and in some countries rose as high as 33%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frank_Bernanke_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frank_Bernanke-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cities_in_the_Great_Depression" title="Cities in the Great Depression">Cities around the world were hit</a> hard, especially those dependent on <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a>. Construction was virtually halted in many countries. Farming communities and rural areas suffered as crop prices fell by about 60%.<sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USBLS_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-USBLS-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></sup> Faced with plummeting demand and few job alternatives, areas dependent on <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Primary sector of the economy">primary sector industries</a> suffered the most.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Economic historians usually consider the catalyst of the Great Depression to be the sudden devastating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Tuesday" title="Black Tuesday">collapse of U.S. stock market prices</a>, starting on October 24, 1929. However, some dispute this conclusion, seeing the stock crash less as a cause of the Depression and more as a symptom of the rising nervousness of investors partly due to gradual price declines caused by falling sales of consumer goods (as a result of overproduction because of new production techniques, falling exports and income inequality, among other factors) that had already been underway as part of a gradual Depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frank_Bernanke_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Frank_Bernanke-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>

</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span></h2>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a> dropped from 381 to 198 over the course of two months, optimism persisted for some time. The stock market rose in early 1930, with the Dow returning to 294 (pre-depression levels) in April 1930, before steadily declining for years, to a low of 41 in 1932.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the beginning, governments and businesses spent more in the first half of 1930 than in the corresponding period of the previous year. On the other hand, consumers, many of whom suffered severe losses in the stock market the previous year, cut  expenditures by 10%. In addition, beginning in the mid-1930s, a <a href="/wiki/Dust_Bowl" title="Dust Bowl">severe drought</a> ravaged the agricultural heartland of the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drought_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-drought-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>Interest rates dropped to low levels by mid-1930, but expected <a href="/wiki/Deflation" title="Deflation">deflation</a> and the continuing reluctance of people to borrow meant that consumer spending and investment remained low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> By May 1930, automobile sales declined to below the levels of 1928. Prices, in general, began to decline, although wages held steady in 1930. Then a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deflationary_spiral" title="Deflationary spiral">deflationary spiral</a> started in 1931. Farmers faced a worse outlook; declining crop prices and a Great Plains drought crippled their economic outlook. At its peak, the Great Depression saw nearly 10% of all Great Plains farms change hands despite federal assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>The decline in the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States" title="Economy of the United States">U.S. economy</a> was the factor that pulled down most other countries at first; then, internal weaknesses or strengths in each country made conditions worse or better.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Frantic attempts by individual countries to shore up their economies through <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionist</a> policies – such as the 1930 U.S. <a href="/wiki/Smoot%E2%80%93Hawley_Tariff_Act" title="Smoot–Hawley Tariff Act">Smoot–Hawley Tariff Act</a> and retaliatory tariffs in other countries – exacerbated the collapse in global trade, contributing to the depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> By 1933, the economic decline pushed world trade to one third of its level compared to four years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
